تعالى بوساطة (أ) (ب)، وبوساطة (ب) (ج)، وبوساطة (أ ب) معا (د) و (ج) في مرتبة واحدة، وبوساطة (د) معلول، وبوساطة (ج) ثان، وبوساطة (د) ثالث، وبوساطة (د ب) رابع، وبوساطة (دج) خامس، وبوساطة (ج أ) سادس، وبوساطة (ج) (ب) سابع، وبوساطة (أ ب ج) ثامن، وبوساطة (أ ب د) تاسع، وبوساطة (أ ب ج) عاشر. وهذه العشرة في مرتبة، وهكذا بالغا ما بلغ. وقالوا جميعا لربط الحادث بالقديم إن حركة الفلك أزلية أبدية متجددة، فهي ذات جهتين، فمن جهة دوامها فاضت عن القديم، ومن جهة التجدد صارت واسطة بين الحوادث وبين الله تعالى في وصول الفيض. فإن قيل فما علة التجدد؟ قالوا تجددها لذاتها، لا يحتاج إلى جعل جاعل أصلا. فإن قيل: أجزاء الحركة حادثة، فلها علة، فإما قديمة، فيلزم قدمها، وإما حادثة، فلا بد لها من علة حادثة، وهكذا، فإما يلزم قدم أجزاء الحركة أو التسلسل. أجيب بأن أجزاءها غير موجودة لاتصالها فلا تحتاج إلى جعل جاعل، فورد عليهم إشكال بأن الحركة غير قارة فلا تستند إلى ثابت، فلا بد علة لها نحو من عدم القرار فيتسلسل العلل. فلدفع ذلك قالوا: إن ههنا ثلاث سلاسل: الأولى من التخييلات الجزئية، والثانية من الإرادات والأشواق، والثالثة من الدورات. فواحد من التخييل علة موجبة لشوق واردة، علة معدة لدورة، وهي معدة لتخييل آخر، وهو موجب لشوق واردة أخرى، وهي معدة لدورة أخرى. فسلسلة الحركة فاضت من سلسلة الإرادات والأشواق، وهي غير قارة، وهي فاضت من سلسلة التخييلات، أيضا غير قارة، وهي فاضت من الحركة من غير لزوم دور، كما بينا، وبه اندفع الاعتراض الثاني أيضا. وفيه نظر؛ لأن الدورة التي فاضت عن إرادة جزئية فائضة عن تخيل جزئي إما علة موجبة لتخييل آخر، فيجب اجتماعها معه، وكذا مع معلوله ومعلول معلوله، فيلزم اجتماع أجزاء الحركة، وإما معدة، فلا بد أن لا سلسلة المعدات إلى واجب الوجود بالذات، وإلا لزم قدمها، فلم يجب وجود واحد منها؛ لأن الواجب ما يمتنع عليه جميع أنحاء العدم، ومن بعض عدم تلك السلسلة بأجمعها وهو ممكن فيلزم أن لا يكون موجودا؛ لأن الشيء ما لم يجب لم يوجد. ومن ههنا سقط ما قيل في ربط الحادث بالقديم من إسقاط وساطة الحركة، والقول بأن وجود كل حادث مسبوق بوجود حادث قبله معد له، وهكذا إلى غير النهاية، والله أعلم. وبسط القول في «العجالة النافعة».
Unlimited [effects], so they must have many causes likewise, and those directions are limited. Indeed the Peripatetics also did not definitively decide that the intellects are ten or twenty, and that the spheres are nine. So the method according to their view is: from Him Most High originated an effect, let it be (A), and from Him Most High through mediation of (A) [came] (B), and through mediation of (B) [came] (C), and through mediation of (A and B) together (D) and (C) in one order, and through mediation of (D) an effect, and through mediation of (C) a second, and through mediation of (D) a third, and through mediation of (D and B) a fourth, and through mediation of (D and C) a fifth, and through mediation of (C and A) a sixth, and through mediation of (C) and (B) a seventh, and through mediation of (A, B, C) an eighth, and through mediation of (A, B, D) a ninth, and through mediation of (A, B, C) a tenth. And these ten are in one order, and so on ad infinitum. And they all said, for linking the temporal to the eternal: the motion of the sphere is eternal, perpetual, and renewing, so it has two aspects: from the aspect of its perpetuity it emanated from the Eternal, and from the aspect of renewal it became an intermediary between temporal events and God Most High in the arrival of emanation. If it is said: what is the cause of renewal? They said: its renewal is from its essence, it does not need any maker at all. If it is said: the parts of motion are temporal, so they have a cause. Either [that cause is] eternal, then their eternality is entailed, or temporal, then they must have a temporal cause, and so on, so either the eternality of the parts of motion or infinite regress is entailed. It was answered: its parts are non-existent because of their continuity, so they do not need a maker. Then an objection was raised against them: motion is non-stable, so it cannot be based on something stable; so it must have a cause of a kind of non-stability, so the causes would regress infinitely. To repel that, they said: There are three chains here: the first of partial imaginings, the second of wills and yearnings, and the third of rotations. So a single imagining is an obligating cause for a yearning, [which is] an efficient cause for a rotation, and it [the rotation] is an efficient cause for another imagining, and it is obligating for a yearning, [which is] an efficient cause for another rotation. So the chain of motion emanated from the chain of wills and yearnings, which is non-stable, and it emanated from the chain of imaginings, also non-stable, and it emanated from motion without circularity, as we have explained, and by this the second objection is also repelled. But there is a consideration in it: because the rotation that emanated from a partial will emanating from a partial imagining: either it is an obligating cause for another imagining, so it must coexist with it, and likewise with its effect and the effect of its effect, so coexistence of the parts of motion is entailed; or it is an efficient cause, then the chain of efficient causes must end with the Necessary Existence by essence, otherwise their eternality would be entailed; then the existence of any one of them would not be necessary, because the necessary is that all aspects of non-existence are impossible for it. And some non-existence of that entire chain is possible, so it would entail that it does not exist; because a thing, as long as it is not necessary, it does not exist. And from this, what was said regarding linking the temporal to the eternal by dropping the intermediary of motion and the statement that the existence of every temporal event is preceded by the existence of a temporal event before it that prepares for it, and so on ad infinitum, falls away. And Allah knows best. And the expansion of the statement is in 'al-'Ujalah al-Nafi'ah'.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents a critique of the Peripatetic (Aristotelian) scheme of emanation and their attempt to connect the temporal universe with the eternal God through the movement of the spheres. The author begins by noting that the causes are unlimited, but the directions are limited, and the Peripatetics were not certain about the exact number of intellects or spheres. He then describes their emanation scheme using letter variables (أ, ب, ج, د) to represent successive intellects emanating from God, generating a series of effects. They claim that the motion of the sphere is both eternal and renewing, serving as a bridge between the eternal and the temporal. The author then raises an objection: what causes the renewal of motion? They reply that it is self-renewing, needing no creator. A second objection is raised: the parts of motion are temporal, so they require a cause, leading to an infinite regress or pre-eternity of parts. They respond that the parts are non-existent due to continuity, so no cause is needed. Then a further objection: motion is non-stable, so it cannot depend on something stable, leading to regress. To avoid this, they propose three chains: imaginings, wills/yearnings, and rotations, where each chain emanates from the previous without circularity. The author then criticizes this: either the rotation is an obligating cause for the next imagining, leading to coexistence of all parts of motion, or it is an efficient cause, which requires the chain to end with the Necessary Being, otherwise the chain would be eternal and the existence of any member would not be necessary since the whole chain could be non-existent. This critique undermines the entire scheme of linking the temporal to the eternal through motion. The author concludes that this view is invalid and refers to 'al-Ujalah al-Nafi’ah' for a fuller discussion.

علة
تخييل

دورة

Key Takeaway
The three-chain theory is refuted by a dilemma: the causal link between rotation and imagining either forces all motions to coexist or leaves the entire chain contingent, thus failing to connect the temporal to the eternal.

The Theologians' View on Delay of Effect from a Complete Cause
Author presents the mutakallimun's position that the effect may lag behind the complete cause when the agent is free.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the mutakallimun's justification for the delay of effect from a complete cause and identify how it avoids the problem of preponderance without a preponderant.

Core Idea
Effect can lag behind a complete cause if the cause is a free agent—no external preponderant needed.

Theologians (mutakallimun) defend the possibility of an effect being delayed even when its cause is complete, as long as the cause is a free agent. They argue this does not violate the principle of sufficient reason because the preponderance arises from the agent's own choice, not an external preponderant. This passage presents two versions of their view, both reconciling divine freedom with causal efficacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions
First opinion: delay allowed with free agent, preponderance is from the agent's choice. Second opinion: effect is impossible in some time of cause, so cause's influence delayed, and possibility is abstract.
2
Understand the logical problem
Without free agent, complete cause necessitates immediate effect; delay would require a preponderant, leading to infinite regress or violation of the principle.
3
Analyze the first solution
The preponderance is not from an external preponderant but from the agent's own choice, thus no tarjih bila murajjih.
4
Analyze the second solution
Possibility (imkan) is part of the complete cause; it is an abstract notion, so it does not require existence. The cause's influence does not reach the effect in that time because the effect is impossible (unready), but possibility is abstract, so no contradiction.
5
Compare to philosophical view
Philosophers hold that complete cause necessitates effect immediately; theologians reject this to preserve divine freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنحائه الثاني مذهب المتكلمين: اعلم أنهم جوزوا تخلف المعلول عن العلة التامة، إذا كانت فاعلا مختارا، ولا يلزم الترجيح من غير مرجح؛ لأن الرجحان الذي جاء من قبلها إنما هو رجحان الوجود التخلف. ومنهم من قال: إن من الجائز امتناع المعلول في بعض زمان العلة، فلا يصل تأثير العلة إليه في ذلك الزمان، فلا يوجد إلا بعد ذلك، ولا يلزم خرق فرض تمام العلة؛ لدخول الإمكان فيها؛ لأن الإمكان أمر انتزاعي معدوم إلا بعد الانتزاع، فكيف يحتاج إليه موجود؟
Its second aspect: the school of the theologians. Know that they allowed the effect to lag behind the complete cause, if it is a free agent. And it does not entail preponderance without a preponderant, because the preponderance that comes from it is only the preponderance of existence over delay. And some of them said: It is possible for the effect to be impossible in some time of the cause, so the cause's influence does not reach it at that time, so it only exists after that. And it does not entail breaking the assumption of the complete cause, because possibility enters into it; because possibility is an abstractive matter, non-existent except after abstraction, so how could an existent need it?
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage presents the theological (mutakallimun) view on the temporal relationship between a cause and its effect. The author identifies two opinions within the school. First, the effect may be delayed relative to the complete cause when the agent is free (mukhtar). This delay does not violate the principle of sufficient reason because the preponderance (tarjih) is not from a preponderant but from the agent's own choice. Second, some theologians hold that the effect is impossible in some time of the cause's existence, so the cause does not produce its effect in that time, and the effect appears later. This does not contradict the concept of the complete cause (al-‘illah al-tammah) because possibility (imkan) is included in that concept, and possibility is an abstract notion that does not exist concretely, so it cannot be a real requirement. Thus, the theologians reconcile divine freedom with causal efficacy.

Key Terms
علة تامة (illa tamma): A complete cause with all conditions present, yet the effect may still be delayed if the agent is free. [Note: Standard term in kalam; differs from philosophical 'illa tamma' which requires immediate effect.]
فاعل مختار (fa'il mukhtar): A free agent who can choose to delay the effect, avoiding the need for an external preponderant. [Note: Stable concept in Islamic theology vs. deterministic philosophy.]
ترجيح بلا مرجح (tarjih bila murajjih): Preponderance without a preponderant, a problem avoided by the theologians' view. [Note: Classical problem in kalam; refuted by the Ash'arite notion of custom.]
إمكان (imkan): Possibility, an abstract property that does not exist in reality but is included in the complete cause. [Note: In philosophy, imkan is a real attribute; here it is 'i'tibari' (abstract).]
انتزاعي (i'tibari): Abstractive, mind-dependent, as opposed to real existence. [Note: Common term in later Islamic thought for mental constructs.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mutakallimun, why does the delay of the effect not require a preponderant?
A) Because the cause is incomplete.
B) Because the preponderance comes from the free agent's choice.
C) Because the effect is eternal.
D) Because possibility is a real attribute that intervenes.

Key Takeaway
The theologians reconcile complete causality with divine freedom by arguing that a free agent's choice itself provides the preponderance, making an external preponderant unnecessary.

The Dialectical Refutation of Time as a Real Entity in Kalam
Author argues that all contingent things depend on God's will and refutes an objection about temporal determination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the dialectical exchange about time and divine will, and refute the objection that a determinant is needed for God's specific timing of creation.

Core Idea
Time is mental, so no prior moment requires a determinant for God's will.

Kalam theologians defend the temporal origination of the world against philosophical objections. A key objection is that if God willed to create the world at a specific moment, there must be a reason for that moment over another. This lesson unpacks the refutation that time itself is not a real entity, thus dissolving the need for a determinant. By mastering this dialectical move, you will strengthen your grasp of how Islamic theology uses logical reasoning to counter skeptical doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main thesis
Find the sentence where the author states that all contingent things depend on God the Desiring, the Chooser. This is the claim being defended.
The author also notes that the effect may lag due to the will's attachment or because it was not possible in pre-eternity.
2
Extract the objection (mu'tarid)
Look for the phrase 'فإن قلت' (if you say). The objector demands a determinant (murjih) for God's will to attach to a specific time within pre-eternity.
The objection assumes time is a real framework within which actions are located.
3
Analyze the author's response (jawab)
The author denies that time is an existing thing; it is an imagined construct from progressions and regressions of contingent things. Before the effect's existence, there is no extended time, so no determinant is needed.
This is the crux: by denying the reality of time, the need for a determinant vanishes.
4
Assess the dialectical outcome
The author declares this a great principle for proving the temporal origination of the world and advises ignoring philosophical objections. Determine whether the refutation succeeds on its own terms.
The refutation hinges on the ontological status of time—a central issue in Kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما منشأ انتزاعه فذات المعلول ، فلو كان علة لكانت علة لنفسها. وبعد تمهيد ذلك فنقول : جميع الممكنات مستندة إلى الله تعالى المريد المختار ابتداءً، ويتخلف المعلول عنه لتعلق إرادته بوجوده كذلك، أو لأن الممكن المعلول لم يكن ممكنا في الأزل؛ بناء على ما سيجيئ إن شاء الله تعالى من أن أزلية الإمكان غير مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية، وغير القار أيضا مستند إليه سبحانه ؛ لتلعق إرادته كذلك، أو لعدم إمكانه إلا كذلك، لكن المختار هو الأول ؛ كما يشهد به قوله تعالى : (۱). فإن قلت: لا بد لترجيح تعلق الإرادة في الأزل بأن يوجد المعلول في وقت معين من اللايزال من مرجح؟ قلت: ليس الزمان أمرا موجودا (۲) ، بل أمرا متوهما من تقدمات وتأخرات عرَضَتْ الممكناتِ، فالواجب سبحانه أراد أن يوجد المعلول بعد العدم، فإذا وجد كذلك يتوهم المتوهم من تقدم عدم على وجود زمانا موهوما، وأما قبله فلا وقت ممتد حتى يطلب الترجيح، فتأمل فيه، هذا أصل عظيم به يفتح باب حدوث العالم الذي هو مسألة عظيمة عندهم، فاحفظه لتأمن عن الوساوس الشيطانية، ولا تلتفت إلى ما قيل من قبل الفلاسفة أو يقال ، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب.
And as for the origin of its derivation, it is the essence of the effect, for if it were a cause, it would be a cause of itself. After prefacing that, we say: All contingent things are dependent upon God the Desiring, the Chooser, from the beginning, and the effect lags behind Him because His will attaches to its existence in such a manner, or because the contingent effect was not possible in pre-eternity, based on what will come, God willing, that the pre-eternity of possibility does not entail the possibility of pre-eternity. And that which is not permanent is also dependent upon Him the Exalted, because His will attaches to it in such a manner, or because it is not possible except in such a manner. But the chosen one is the first, as His statement witnesses: (1). If you say: There must be a determinant for the attachment of the will in pre-eternity to bring the effect into existence at a specific time in the realm of endless duration? I say: Time is not an existing thing (2), but rather an imagined thing consisting of progressions and regressions that befall contingent things. So the Necessary, the Exalted, willed to bring the effect into existence after non-existence. When it exists thus, the imaginer imagines from the priority of non-existence over existence an imagined time. But before that there is no extended time so that a determinant be sought. So reflect on this. This is a great principle by which the door to the temporal origination of the world, which is a great issue with them, is opened. So memorize it to be safe from satanic whisperings, and pay no attention to what the philosophers have said or may say. This, and God knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about causality and divine will. The author begins by stating that if the effect were the cause of itself, it would be absurd. He then asserts that all contingent things are directly caused by God, who is willing and chooses. The effect may be delayed due to the will's specific attachment or because the effect was not possible in pre-eternity. The author prefers the first explanation, citing a verse (footnoted). An objection is then raised: what determines God's will to create the effect at a specific time rather than another? The answer is that time is not a real entity but a mental construct arising from the progressions and regressions that occur to contingent things. Since there is no real time before the effect's existence, no determinant is needed. The author emphasizes this as a key principle for understanding the temporal origination of the world and advises memorizing it to avoid skeptical doubts.

الممكنات
الإرادة
الزمان

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the need for a determinant by denying the reality of time, thus defending the temporal origination of the world against philosophical doubts.

Refuting the Denial of God as Sole Creator
Author critiques philosophers, theologians, and Sufis while refuting Mu'tazila and Shi'a on creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and critique the logical and theological flaws in the Mu'tazila and Shi'a positions on creation using the author's arguments.

Core Idea
Consensus affirms God as sole Creator; apparent causes are mere conditions, not independent agents.

In this passage, the author affirms the Sunni position that only God creates and critiques those who assign creative power to humans. He identifies the Mu'tazila and Shi'a as deviants and supports his refutation with Quranic evidence. Let us dissect the logical structure of this critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's target positions
The author explicitly excludes the Mu'tazila (all human actions) and the Shi'a (evil actions) from the consensus. Note the precise scope: Mu'tazila claim humans independently create all actions; Shi'a claim humans independently create evil actions.
The Magian comparison implies dualism – attributing creation to two sources.
2
Understand the author's grounds for rejection
The author relies on three grounds: (1) consensus of philosophers, theologians, and Sufis; (2) sound conscience (al-wijdān al-salīm) that possibility lacks influence; (3) decisive Quranic proofs.
Sound conscience refers to innate human recognition that only the necessary being can create.
3
Analyze the Quranic proofs cited
The author quotes 'And He created everything' (6:102, 39:6) and 'And God created you and what you do' (37:96). Examine how these verses affirm universal creation and specifically include human actions.
Verse 37:96 is a direct refutation of human independent creation.
4
Evaluate the strength of the critique
The author's argument is based on authoritative consensus and unambiguous revelation. The internal logic is sound: if God creates everything, then nothing else creates independently. The comparison to Magians strengthens the refutation by highlighting the dualist implication.
This critique is foundational in Sunni Kalam; the author's position aligns with Ash'ari/Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الفلاسفة والمتكلمين والصوفية الصافية - كثرهم الله تعالى - على أن لا خالق إلا الله ، وما يرى في الظاهر عللا إنما هي شرائط وروابط إلى الخالق جل ذكره، إلا المعتزلة - خذلهم الله تعالى ـ في أفعال العباد مطلقا، والشيعة الشنيعة في الشرور الصادرة عن العباد، وهذا الرأي يشبه برأي المجوس. ومع شهادة الوجدان السليم أن الإمكان ليس فيه جهة التأثير لنا قاطعة من الكلام الإلهي عليه، نحو: ﴿وَخَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ ﴾ [الأنعام / ۱۰۲ ، والزمر / ٦] ، هو الله (۲) ﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات/ ٩٦] إلى غير ذلك. وإن شئت مزيد تفصيل فارجع إلى شرحنا الفارسي للفقه الأكبر».
And know that the philosophers, the theologians, and the pure Sufis - may God multiply them - are upon [the belief] that there is no creator except God, and what is seen outwardly as causes are only conditions and links to the Creator, the Exalted, except the Mu'tazila - may God forsake them - concerning the actions of the servants absolutely, and the vile Shia concerning the evils emanating from the servants. This opinion resembles the opinion of the Magians. And with the testimony of sound conscience that possibility has no aspect of influence for us, we have decisive proofs from divine speech upon it, such as: 'And He created everything' [Quran 6:102, 39:6], 'He is God' and 'And God created you and what you do' [Quran 37:96], etc. And if you desire more detail, refer to our Persian commentary on al-Fiqh al-Akbar.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This is a critical refutation passage. The author states that philosophers, theologians (presumably Sunni), and pure Sufis agree that only God creates, and apparent causes are merely conditions and links to God. The exception is the Mu'tazila regarding all human actions, and the Shia regarding evil actions from humans. This view is likened to dualist Magians. The author then appeals to sound conscience and Quranic verses as decisive proofs, quoting 'And God created you and what you do' among others. He directs for more detail to his Persian commentary on al-Fiqh al-Akbar.

Key Terms
العلل (al-'ilal): Apparent causes that are actually only conditions and links to the sole Creator. [Note: In philosophical contexts, 'illa often means a real efficient cause; here it is denied real causal efficacy.]
شرائط وروابط (sharā'iṭ wa rawābiṭ): Conditions and connections that mediate between God and created effects, not independent causes. [Note: Specific to this theological context.]

Illuminationist Argument: Existence as Mental Consideration
Author presents Illuminationist first proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the Illuminationist reductio ad absurdum argument against existence being an additive attribute and identify the conditional reasoning used.

Core Idea
Existence cannot be an additive attribute without absurd priority of essence over its own existence.

The Illuminationists argue that existence is merely a mental consideration, not an external attribute added to essence. Their first proof uses a conditional chain: if existence were additive or abstracted, it would lead to absurdities such as essence being prior to its own existence. This reasoning is a classic reductio that you will learn to dissect.

Guided Path
1
State the Illuminationist claim
Identify that the Illuminationists hold existence to be a mental consideration (i'tibari 'aqli).
2
Extract the conditional alternatives
The argument presents cases: existence is either additive (indimami), abstracted (intiza'i), or something disparate (mubayin). Each leads to absurdity.
3
Analyze the additive case
If additive, essence would have to be prior to its own existence, which is impossible. This is the key reductio.
The term 'priority' here is existential priority, not temporal.
4
Identify the conclusion
Therefore, existence must be a mental consideration, and essence is in itself in need of a maker for its determination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذهب الإشراقية إلى الأول، فعندهم كانت الماهية بنفسها في بقعة الليس، فأخرجها الجاعل إلى الأيس. والمشاؤون إلى الثاني، والمراد بالاتصاف بالوجود مفاد قولنا الماهية موجودة. منشأ أن يكون حقية المذهب الأول من الفطريات، وقد يستدل عليه بوجوه: الأول أن الوجود أمر اعتباري عقلي ومصداق حمله نفس تقرر الماهية، فيكون ثبوته للماهية ضروريا، وإلا فهو أمر انتزاعي، فلا بد من له هو المصداق حقيقة، أو انضمامي، فيلزم تقدم الماهية بالوجود على مصداقه، أو أمر مباين، وهو بين الاستحالة. فلو لم يكن الماهية في تقررها محتاجة إلى الجاعل لارتفع الجعل رأسا؛ لأن الوجود صار من اللوازم التي لا تعلل بجعل مستأنف. الثاني أن جعل النسبة التي من المعاني الحرفية غير معقول إلا باعتبار مصداقها الذي هو مفاد الهيئة التركيبية، والمصداق إما نفس الماهية بلا حيثية، فتكون هي المجعولة حقيقة، أو حيثية الاستناد إلى الجاعل، وليس إلا اتباع الماهية للجاعل في الوجود، فيكون بعد صيرورتها موجودة، فكيف يكون مصداقا لها، أو مع حيثية أخرى انضمامية أو انتزاعية، وكل صفة انضمامية أو انتزاعية متأخرة عن وجود المعروض، ولا أقل أن يكون معه، فكيف يكون مصداقا لحمل الوجود؟ وبالجملة ليس سوى الماهية قابلا للمصداقية حتى يجعل، وما قيل إن النسبة لها وجود في الأعيان، وكذا سائر الانتزاعيات، وإلا لزم ارتفاع النقيضين؛ لأنهما قد يكونان انتزاعيين فخارج عن دائرة العقل، وارتفاع النقيضين بمعنى أن لا يكون واحد منهما مطابقا لما حكى عنه مستحيل، لا أن لا يكونا معدومين عن الأعيان، كيف ولو كان للانتزاعيات وجود سوى وجود المصداق لزم كون الواجب تعالى محلا للحوادث؛ لحدوث الإضافات يوما فيوما، ويلزم أن يكون شيء واحد موصوفا بصفات غير متناهية؛ لأن الانتزاعيات قد تكون واقفة عند حد، كسلسلة اللزومات مثلا. الثالث: الماهية إما محتاجة إلى الجاعل أولا وبالذات، وهو المطلوب، وإما بالعرض، فيلزم تأخر نفس الماهية عن الماهية الموجودة المتأخرة عن الوجود، أو معه فيلزم تقدم العارض على المعروض أو لا بالعرض ولا بالذات، فيلزم استغناء الماهية عن الجاعل. ويرد عليه أن نفس الماهية باعتبار التقرر عن الجاعل متأخرة عن الماهية الموجودة، متقدمة عليها بنحو آخر من التقدم، ولا استحالة في أن يكون المتأخر باعتبار متقدما باعتبار آخر. وأيضا لو كان بينهما معية لما لزم تقدم العارض على المعروض؛ لأن ما مع المتقدم بالذات لا يجب أن يكون متقدما، العلة غير مستحيل؛ لأنها غير ممكنة عندهم؛ إذ على أن استغناء الماهية عن المواد الثلاثة كيفيات للنسبة، فتأمل. قال أتباع المشائين أولا: لا يمكن تعلق الجعل بالماهية، وإلا لزم المجعولية الذاتية، ولا بالوجود؛ لكونه صفة انتزاعية، فلا بد أن يتعلق باتصافها بالوجود، وإلا ارتفع الجعل رأسا. ويرد عليه أولا أن الاتصاف أيضا انتزاعي. فإن قلت: مفاده أمر عيني؟ قلت: هو نفس الماهية، كما بينا في الدليل الثاني.
The Illuminationists adopted the first view; according to them, the essence in itself was in the realm of non-existence, then the maker brought it out to existence. The Peripatetics adopted the second view, and what is meant by being qualified by existence is the meaning of our statement 'the essence exists'. The origin of the first doctrine being a primitive truth may be argued by proofs: First, that existence is a mental consideration and the referent of its predication is the very determination of the essence, so its being affirmed of the essence is necessary. Otherwise, it is an abstracted matter, so it must have a real referent, or it is an additive, entailing the priority of essence with existence over its referent, or it is something disparate, and that is clearly impossible. So were the essence not in its determination in need of the maker, making would be entirely eliminated; because existence would become a necessary property not requiring a fresh making. Second, that making a relation, which is from among the meanings of particles, is unintelligible except by considering its referent, which is the meaning of the composite form. The referent is either the essence itself without any qualification, so it is the real made thing, or it is the qualification of dependence on the maker, which is nothing but the essence's following the maker in existence, so it would be after it becomes existent, so how could it be a referent for it? Or it is with another additive or abstracted qualification, and every additive or abstracted quality is posterior to the existence of the subject, or at least simultaneous with it, so how could it be a referent for the predication of existence? In short, there is nothing other than the essence capable of being a referent so that it could be made. And what is said that the relation has a concrete existence, and likewise all abstracted matters, otherwise the two contradictories would be eliminated, because they may be abstracted and outside the circle of the intellect. The elimination of the two contradictories in the sense that neither of them corresponds to what is reported about it is impossible, not that they are not non-existent in concrete things. Consider: had the abstracted matters an existence other than the existence of the referent, it would necessitate the Necessary Being being a locus of accidents, because relations arise day by day, and it would necessitate one thing being described with infinite attributes, because abstracted matters can be infinite, such as the chain of implications. Third: The essence is either in need of the maker primarily and essentially, which is what is sought; or accidentally, entailing the posteriority of the essence itself to the existing essence which is posterior to existence, or simultaneous with it, entailing the priority of the accident over the subject; or neither accidentally nor essentially, entailing the essence's independence of the maker. Reply: The essence itself, in terms of determination by the maker, is posterior to the existing essence, yet prior to it in another aspect, and there is no impossibility in something being posterior in one respect and prior in another. Also, if there were simultaneity between them, it would not necessitate priority of the accident over the subject, because what is simultaneous with what is essentially prior is not necessarily prior. The cause is not impossible, because it is not possible according to them, since the essence's independence of the three materials is a quality of the relation, so reflect. The followers of the Peripatetics said: First, it is not possible for making to attach to the essence, otherwise self-made would follow, nor to existence because it is an abstracted attribute, so it must attach to its being qualified by existence, otherwise making would be entirely eliminated. Reply: First, being qualified is also abstracted. If you say: its content is a concrete thing? I say: it is the essence itself, as we showed in the second proof.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange between the Illuminationist and Peripatetic schools regarding the nature of existence (wujud) and its relation to essence (mahiyya). The author, commenting on the matn of Sullam al-Ulum, begins by stating the two positions: the Illuminationists hold that existence is a mental consideration, while the Peripatetics hold that existence is an attribute added to essence. The author then presents three proofs for the Illuminationist view, followed by a refutation, and then a new objection from the Peripatetic followers with a subsequent reply.

First Proof: Existence is a mental consideration. If it were otherwise—either an abstracted (intiza'i) or additive (indimami) property—it would lead to absurdities such as priority of essence over its referent. If essence were not in need of the maker, then existence would be a necessary concomitant not requiring a special act of making.

Second Proof: The making (ja'l) of a relational entity is unintelligible without a concrete referent. That referent can only be the essence itself, not a qualification that is posterior to existence. If abstracted matters had concrete existence independent of their referents, God would be subject to accidents, and an infinite regress would follow.

Third Proof: The essence must be either essentially or accidentally in need of the maker. The first is the desired conclusion; the second leads to posteriority of essence; the third leads to essence's independence. A reply is given: the same essence can be posterior in one respect and prior in another, thus avoiding the alleged contradictions.

Finally, the Peripatetic followers object that making cannot attach to essence (to avoid self-making) nor to existence (an abstracted attribute), so it must attach to the qualification of essence by existence. The author replies that qualification is also abstracted, and its concrete content is the essence itself, as was shown in the second proof.

Key Terms
الماهية
الوجود
الجعل
الاتصاف
الانتزاعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Illuminationist first proof, what is the consequence if existence were additive (indimami)?
A) Essence would be eternal.
B) Essence would be prior to its own existence.
C) The maker would be unnecessary.
D) Existence would be a mental consideration.

Key Takeaway
The Illuminationist reductio shows that positing existence as an external attribute leads to logical absurdity, forcing the conclusion that existence is a mental consideration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a similar reductio argument against the claim that 'property (milk) in a contract is an independent entity added to the object of sale.' Use the conditional form: if it were independent, it would lead to absurdity X.

Peripatetic Objection and Dialectical Exchange on Making
Author presents Peripatetic objection and Illuminationist reply

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to map the dialectical exchange between the Peripatetics and Illuminationists on the object of making (ja'l) and evaluate the validity of the Peripatetic disjunctive syllogism.

Core Idea
The Peripatetics use a disjunctive argument to force the conclusion that making attaches to the qualification, but the reply shows that qualification is also abstracted.

The Peripatetics object that making cannot attach to essence (self-making) nor to existence (abstracted), so it must attach to the qualification of essence by existence. The reply counters that qualification is itself abstracted, and its concrete content is the essence. This exchange illustrates a critical dialectical move.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Peripatetic claim
Making must attach to something; it cannot be essence or existence.
2
Reconstruct the disjunctive syllogism
The options are: essence, existence, or the qualification. First two eliminated, so qualification remains.
This is a standard disjunctive syllogism.
3
Analyze the Illuminationist reply
The reply says qualification is abstracted, so the same problem recurs; the concrete referent is essence itself.
4
Determine the dialectical outcome
The Illuminationists effectively block the Peripatetic move by showing the qualification is not a concrete thing.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فذهب الإشراقية إلى الأول، فعندهم كانت الماهية بنفسها في بقعة الليس، فأخرجها الجاعل إلى الأيس. والمشاؤون إلى الثاني، والمراد بالاتصاف بالوجود مفاد قولنا الماهية موجودة. منشأ أن يكون حقية المذهب الأول من الفطريات، وقد يستدل عليه بوجوه: الأول أن الوجود أمر اعتباري عقلي ومصداق حمله نفس تقرر الماهية، فيكون ثبوته للماهية ضروريا، وإلا فهو أمر انتزاعي، فلا بد من له هو المصداق حقيقة، أو انضمامي، فيلزم تقدم الماهية بالوجود على مصداقه، أو أمر مباين، وهو بين الاستحالة. فلو لم يكن الماهية في تقررها محتاجة إلى الجاعل لارتفع الجعل رأسا؛ لأن الوجود صار من اللوازم التي لا تعلل بجعل مستأنف. الثاني أن جعل النسبة التي من المعاني الحرفية غير معقول إلا باعتبار مصداقها الذي هو مفاد الهيئة التركيبية، والمصداق إما نفس الماهية بلا حيثية، فتكون هي المجعولة حقيقة، أو حيثية الاستناد إلى الجاعل، وليس إلا اتباع الماهية للجاعل في الوجود، فيكون بعد صيرورتها موجودة، فكيف يكون مصداقا لها، أو مع حيثية أخرى انضمامية أو انتزاعية، وكل صفة انضمامية أو انتزاعية متأخرة عن وجود المعروض، ولا أقل أن يكون معه، فكيف يكون مصداقا لحمل الوجود؟ وبالجملة ليس سوى الماهية قابلا للمصداقية حتى يجعل، وما قيل إن النسبة لها وجود في الأعيان، وكذا سائر الانتزاعيات، وإلا لزم ارتفاع النقيضين؛ لأنهما قد يكونان انتزاعيين فخارج عن دائرة العقل، وارتفاع النقيضين بمعنى أن لا يكون واحد منهما مطابقا لما حكى عنه مستحيل، لا أن لا يكونا معدومين عن الأعيان، كيف ولو كان للانتزاعيات وجود سوى وجود المصداق لزم كون الواجب تعالى محلا للحوادث؛ لحدوث الإضافات يوما فيوما، ويلزم أن يكون شيء واحد موصوفا بصفات غير متناهية؛ لأن الانتزاعيات قد تكون واقفة عند حد، كسلسلة اللزومات مثلا. الثالث: الماهية إما محتاجة إلى الجاعل أولا وبالذات، وهو المطلوب، وإما بالعرض، فيلزم تأخر نفس الماهية عن الماهية الموجودة المتأخرة عن الوجود، أو معه فيلزم تقدم العارض على المعروض أو لا بالعرض ولا بالذات، فيلزم استغناء الماهية عن الجاعل. ويرد عليه أن نفس الماهية باعتبار التقرر عن الجاعل متأخرة عن الماهية الموجودة، متقدمة عليها بنحو آخر من التقدم، ولا استحالة في أن يكون المتأخر باعتبار متقدما باعتبار آخر. وأيضا لو كان بينهما معية لما لزم تقدم العارض على المعروض؛ لأن ما مع المتقدم بالذات لا يجب أن يكون متقدما، العلة غير مستحيل؛ لأنها غير ممكنة عندهم؛ إذ على أن استغناء الماهية عن المواد الثلاثة كيفيات للنسبة، فتأمل. قال أتباع المشائين أولا: لا يمكن تعلق الجعل بالماهية، وإلا لزم المجعولية الذاتية، ولا بالوجود؛ لكونه صفة انتزاعية، فلا بد أن يتعلق باتصافها بالوجود، وإلا ارتفع الجعل رأسا. ويرد عليه أولا أن الاتصاف أيضا انتزاعي. فإن قلت: مفاده أمر عيني؟ قلت: هو نفس الماهية، كما بينا في الدليل الثاني.
The Illuminationists adopted the first view; according to them, the essence in itself was in the realm of non-existence, then the maker brought it out to existence. The Peripatetics adopted the second view, and what is meant by being qualified by existence is the meaning of our statement 'the essence exists'. The origin of the first doctrine being a primitive truth may be argued by proofs: First, that existence is a mental consideration and the referent of its predication is the very determination of the essence, so its being affirmed of the essence is necessary. Otherwise, it is an abstracted matter, so it must have a real referent, or it is an additive, entailing the priority of essence with existence over its referent, or it is something disparate, and that is clearly impossible. So were the essence not in its determination in need of the maker, making would be entirely eliminated; because existence would become a necessary property not requiring a fresh making. Second, that making a relation, which is from among the meanings of particles, is unintelligible except by considering its referent, which is the meaning of the composite form. The referent is either the essence itself without any qualification, so it is the real made thing, or it is the qualification of dependence on the maker, which is nothing but the essence's following the maker in existence, so it would be after it becomes existent, so how could it be a referent for it? Or it is with another additive or abstracted qualification, and every additive or abstracted quality is posterior to the existence of the subject, or at least simultaneous with it, so how could it be a referent for the predication of existence? In short, there is nothing other than the essence capable of being a referent so that it could be made. And what is said that the relation has a concrete existence, and likewise all abstracted matters, otherwise the two contradictories would be eliminated, because they may be abstracted and outside the circle of the intellect. The elimination of the two contradictories in the sense that neither of them corresponds to what is reported about it is impossible, not that they are not non-existent in concrete things. Consider: had the abstracted matters an existence other than the existence of the referent, it would necessitate the Necessary Being being a locus of accidents, because relations arise day by day, and it would necessitate one thing being described with infinite attributes, because abstracted matters can be infinite, such as the chain of implications. Third: The essence is either in need of the maker primarily and essentially, which is what is sought; or accidentally, entailing the posteriority of the essence itself to the existing essence which is posterior to existence, or simultaneous with it, entailing the priority of the accident over the subject; or neither accidentally nor essentially, entailing the essence's independence of the maker. Reply: The essence itself, in terms of determination by the maker, is posterior to the existing essence, yet prior to it in another aspect, and there is no impossibility in something being posterior in one respect and prior in another. Also, if there were simultaneity between them, it would not necessitate priority of the accident over the subject, because what is simultaneous with what is essentially prior is not necessarily prior. The cause is not impossible, because it is not possible according to them, since the essence's independence of the three materials is a quality of the relation, so reflect. The followers of the Peripatetics said: First, it is not possible for making to attach to the essence, otherwise self-made would follow, nor to existence because it is an abstracted attribute, so it must attach to its being qualified by existence, otherwise making would be entirely eliminated. Reply: First, being qualified is also abstracted. If you say: its content is a concrete thing? I say: it is the essence itself, as we showed in the second proof.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange between the Illuminationist and Peripatetic schools regarding the nature of existence (wujud) and its relation to essence (mahiyya). The author, commenting on the matn of Sullam al-Ulum, begins by stating the two positions: the Illuminationists hold that existence is a mental consideration, while the Peripatetics hold that existence is an attribute added to essence. The author then presents three proofs for the Illuminationist view, followed by a refutation, and then a new objection from the Peripatetic followers with a subsequent reply.

First Proof: Existence is a mental consideration. If it were otherwise—either an abstracted (intiza'i) or additive (indimami) property—it would lead to absurdities such as priority of essence over its referent. If essence were not in need of the maker, then existence would be a necessary concomitant not requiring a special act of making.

Second Proof: The making (ja'l) of a relational entity is unintelligible without a concrete referent. That referent can only be the essence itself, not a qualification that is posterior to existence. If abstracted matters had concrete existence independent of their referents, God would be subject to accidents, and an infinite regress would follow.

Third Proof: The essence must be either essentially or accidentally in need of the maker. The first is the desired conclusion; the second leads to posteriority of essence; the third leads to essence's independence. A reply is given: the same essence can be posterior in one respect and prior in another, thus avoiding the alleged contradictions.

Finally, the Peripatetic followers object that making cannot attach to essence (to avoid self-making) nor to existence (an abstracted attribute), so it must attach to the qualification of essence by existence. The author replies that qualification is also abstracted, and its concrete content is the essence itself, as was shown in the second proof.

Key Terms
الماهية
الوجود
الجعل
الاتصاف
الانتزاعي

Checkpoint
According to the Peripatetic argument, why can making not attach to existence?
A) Existence is eternal.
B) Existence is an abstracted attribute.
C) Existence is the same as essence.
D) Existence is a mental consideration.

Key Takeaway
The Peripatetic disjunctive syllogism is valid, but the Illuminationist reply refutes the third option by showing that 'qualification' is not concrete, thereby preserving their original position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the debate on whether knowledge (ilm) is an accident or a state. Formulate a disjunctive syllogism for why it must be a state, based on elimination of accident and substance.

Refuting the Peripatetic Objection: Creation Cannot Attach to Essence
Author refutes three Peripatetic objections against attaching creation to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the Peripatetic claim that creation cannot attach to essence by distinguishing simple creation from composite creation.

Core Idea
Simple creation makes the essence itself, not an attribute or recipient.

The Peripatetics argued that creation cannot be attached to essence because that would imply essential made-ness, nor to existence because existence is abstract, so it must attach to the attribute of 'being described' by existence. In this lesson, we analyze this objection and the author's reply: 'being described' is also abstract, and the true object of simple creation is the essence itself. This distinction is crucial for understanding Ash'ari theology on divine causation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Peripatetic trilemma
The Peripatetics claim creation cannot attach to essence (otherwise essential made-ness), nor to existence (abstract), so it must attach to the attribute of being described with existence.
2
Notice the author's first reply
The author points out that 'being described' is itself an abstract concept, not concrete, so the trilemma fails.
3
Understand the concept of simple creation
The author distinguishes between composite creation (which requires a recipient) and simple creation (which brings the essence itself into being without a recipient).
4
Apply the distinction
The Peripatetic objection assumes all creation is composite, but simple creation is possible and is the core of the issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الكتاب النقيضين؛ لأنهما قد يكونان انتزاعيين فخارج عن دائرة العقل، وارتفاع النقيضين بمعنى بمعنى، أن لا يكون واحد منهما مطابقا لما حكى عنه مستحيل، لا أن لا يكونا معدومين عن الأعيان، كيف ولو كان للانتزاعيات وجود سوى وجود المصداق لزم كون الواجب تعالى محلا للحوادث ؛ لحدوث الإضافات يوما فيوما، ويلزم أن يكون شيء واحد موصوفا بصفات غير متناهية ؛ لأن الانتزاعيات قد تكون واقفة عند حد، كسلسلة اللزومات مثلا . الثالث: الماهية إما محتاجة إلى الجاعل أولا وبالذات ، وهو المطلوب، وإما بالعرض، فيلزم تأخر نفس الماهية عن الماهية الموجودة المتأخرة عن الوجود، أو معه فيلزم تقدم العارض على المعروض أو لا بالعرض ولا بالذات، فيلزم استغناء الماهية عن الجاعل . ويرد عليه أن نفس الماهية باعتبار التقرر عن الجاعل متأخرة عن الماهية الموجودة، متقدمة عليها بنحو آخر من التقدم، ولا استحالة في أن يكون المتأخر باعتبار متقدما باعتبار آخر. وأيضا لو كان بينهما معية لما لزم تقدم العارض على المعروض ؛ لأن ما مع المتقدم بالذات لا يجب أن يكون متقدما ، العلة غير مستحيل ؛ لأنها غير ممكنة عندهم؛ إذ على أن استغناء الماهية عن المواد الثلاثة كيفيات للنسبة ، فتأمل . قال أتباع المشائين أولا: لا يمكن تعلق الجعل بالماهية، وإلا لزم المجعولية الذاتية، ولا بالوجود ؛ لكونه صفة انتزاعية، فلا بد أن يتعلق باتصافها بالوجود، وإلا ارتفع الجعل رأسا ويرد عليه أولا أن الاتصاف أيضا انتزاعي. فإن قلت: مفاده أمر عيني ؟ قلت: هو نفس الماهية، كما بينا في الدليل الثاني. وثانيا: إن أريد بالمجعولية الذاتية ثبوت نفس الماهية لنفسها ففيه غفلة عن تصور معنى الجعل البسيط ، أو مجعولية مصداقه، وهو نفس الماهية، فلا استحالة فيه، بل هو أصل المسألة. ومن ههنا سقط ما قيل في إثبات لزوم المجعولية الذاتية أن حقيقتها مجعولة بثبوت الذات لنفسها باعتبار المصداق، ومصداقه ليس إلا نفس الماهية ، وقد قلتم إنها مجعولة. وثانيا إن المجعول بالذات ما هو ممكن بالذات، والإمكان كيفية النسبة. ويرد عليه أن المواد الثلاثة عندنا كيفيات نفس تقرر الماهية. وثالثا إن الجعل يستدعي مغايرة المجعول والمجعول إليه، ويرد عليه أن استدعاء المغايرة إنما هو في المؤلف، دون البسيط ؛ فإنه لا يستدعي مجعولا إليه ، فضلا عن المغايرة، والله أعلم.
Introduction of the book: [The impossibility of] the two opposites because they may be abstracted (intiza'i) thus outside the domain of the intellect. The removal of both opposites in the sense that neither one corresponds to what it reports is impossible, not that they are non-existent in external entities. How so? For if abstracted things had existence apart from the existence of the referent, it would entail the Necessary Being being a locus of accidents due to the daily occurrence of relations, and it would entail that one thing is described with infinite attributes because abstracted things may stop at a limit, like the chain of implications for example. Third: The essence is either in need of the creator primarily and essentially—which is what is sought—or accidentally, which entails the posteriority of the essence itself to the existing essence that is posterior to existence, or together with it, which entails the priority of the accident over the subject, or neither accidentally nor essentially, which entails the independence of the essence from the creator. And it is replied that the essence itself, by virtue of being determined by the creator, is posterior to the existing essence and prior to it in another mode of priority, and there is no impossibility in something posterior in one respect being prior in another respect. Also, if there were simultaneity between them, the priority of the accident over the subject would not necessarily follow, because what is simultaneous with what is essentially prior need not be prior. The cause is not impossible because it is not possible according to them; since the independence of the essence from the three modalities as qualities of the relation, so reflect. The followers of the Peripatetics said first: It is impossible to attach creation to essence, otherwise essential made-ness would follow; nor to existence because it is an abstract attribute; so it must be attached to its being described with existence, otherwise creation would be nullified. And it is replied first that being described is also abstract. If you say: Its purport is something concrete? I say: It is the essence itself, as we showed in the second proof. And second: If by essential made-ness is meant the affirmation of the essence itself to itself, then there is neglect of conceiving the meaning of simple creation; or the made-ness of its referent, which is the essence itself, so there is no impossibility in it; rather it is the very point of the issue. And from this falls what was said in establishing the necessity of essential made-ness: that its reality is made by the affirmation of the self to itself in terms of the referent, and its referent is nothing but the essence itself, and you have said that it is made. And second: That which is made in essence is that which is possible in essence, and possibility is a modality of the relation. And it is replied that the three modalities according to us are qualities of the very determination of the essence. And third: Creation requires a distinction between the made and the one to whom it is made, and it is replied that requiring distinction applies to the composite, not the simple; for it does not require a recipient, let alone distinction. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the Peripatetic (Mashsha'i) argument that creation (ja'l) cannot be attributed to essence or existence, but only to the attribute of being described by existence. The author first discusses a preliminary point about abstracted concepts (intiza'iyyat) and the impossibility of both opposites being absent. He then presents the Peripatetic trilemma: essence is either essentially in need of a creator (which is sought), accidentally in need, or not in need—if accidentally, the essence would be posterior to the existing essence; if simultaneously, an accident would precede its subject; if neither, the essence is independent. The author replies that the essence can be prior and posterior in different respects, and simultaneity does not entail priority of accident. Then he reports the Peripatetic claim that creation cannot attach to essence (otherwise essential made-ness) nor to existence (abstract), so it must attach to the 'being described' attribute. The author counters that 'being described' is also abstract, and that if the Peripatetics mean essential made-ness as self-affirmation, they misunderstand simple creation. The true referent of creation is the essence itself. The second Peripatetic point about possibility as a modal relation is rebutted by redefining the three modalities (necessity, possibility, impossibility) as qualities of the essence's determination. The third point about the need for distinction between maker and made is rejected for simple creation, which does not require a recipient. The argument uses technical distinctions familiar in Islamic philosophy and kalām, particularly regarding the nature of existence and essence.

Key Terms
الجعل (al-ja'l): The act of bringing something into existence (creation), often analyzed as simple (basiṭ) involving no recipient. [Note: In Peripatetic philosophy, ja'l often requires a recipient; here it is presented as simple, aligning with Ash'ari occasionalism.]
الماهية (al-māhiyya): Essence or quiddity; what something is in itself, distinct from existence. [Note: Stable term across traditions, but its reality is debated: Ash'ari holds it is the existent itself, while Peripatetics distinguish it from existence.]
المجعولية الذاتية (al-maj'ūliyya al-dhātiyya): The state of being made in one's essence; the author refutes that it implies circularity because simple creation makes the essence itself. [Note: This term is specific to the debate on creation, not commonly used outside metaphysics.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the Peripatetic objection fail when it claims that creation cannot attach to essence?
A) Because creation attaches to existence instead.
B) Because 'being described' is concrete, not abstract.
C) Because simple creation makes the essence itself and does not require a recipient.
D) Because essential made-ness is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The refutation of the Peripatetic objection rests on the distinction between simple creation, which directly makes the essence, and composite creation, which requires a recipient.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a simple argument showing how God's creation of an essence (e.g., the essence of a human) does not require a pre-existing recipient. Use the concept of al-ja'l al-basīṭ.

Refuting the Peripatetic Claim that Possibility is a Modal Relation
Author refutes three Peripatetic objections against attaching creation to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that possibility is merely a relation by explaining that the three modalities are qualities of the essence's determination.

Core Idea
The three modalities are not relations but qualities inherent in the determination of essence.

The Peripatetics argued that the object of creation must be possible in essence, and possibility is a 'quality of the relation'. The author counters that the three modalities (necessity, possibility, impossibility) are qualities of the very determination (taqarrur) of the essence. This lesson unpacks this metaphysical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Peripatetic assertion
The Peripatetics say that the made in essence is what is possible in essence, and possibility is a modal relation.
2
Understand the author's reply
The author asserts that the three modalities according to us (Ash'aris) are qualities of the essence's determination itself, not merely a relation.
3
Contrast the two views
Peripatetics see possibility as a relative attribute; Ash'aris see it as a real quality of the essence.
4
See the implication for creation
If possibility is a quality of essence, then creation directly gives essence its modal status, not just a relation.

مقدمة الكتاب النقيضين؛ لأنهما قد يكونان انتزاعيين فخارج عن دائرة العقل، وارتفاع النقيضين بمعنى بمعنى، أن لا يكون واحد منهما مطابقا لما حكى عنه مستحيل، لا أن لا يكونا معدومين عن الأعيان، كيف ولو كان للانتزاعيات وجود سوى وجود المصداق لزم كون الواجب تعالى محلا للحوادث ؛ لحدوث الإضافات يوما فيوما، ويلزم أن يكون شيء واحد موصوفا بصفات غير متناهية ؛ لأن الانتزاعيات قد تكون واقفة عند حد، كسلسلة اللزومات مثلا . الثالث: الماهية إما محتاجة إلى الجاعل أولا وبالذات ، وهو المطلوب، وإما بالعرض، فيلزم تأخر نفس الماهية عن الماهية الموجودة المتأخرة عن الوجود، أو معه فيلزم تقدم العارض على المعروض أو لا بالعرض ولا بالذات، فيلزم استغناء الماهية عن الجاعل . ويرد عليه أن نفس الماهية باعتبار التقرر عن الجاعل متأخرة عن الماهية الموجودة، متقدمة عليها بنحو آخر من التقدم، ولا استحالة في أن يكون المتأخر باعتبار متقدما باعتبار آخر. وأيضا لو كان بينهما معية لما لزم تقدم العارض على المعروض ؛ لأن ما مع المتقدم بالذات لا يجب أن يكون متقدما ، العلة غير مستحيل ؛ لأنها غير ممكنة عندهم؛ إذ على أن استغناء الماهية عن المواد الثلاثة كيفيات للنسبة ، فتأمل . قال أتباع المشائين أولا: لا يمكن تعلق الجعل بالماهية، وإلا لزم المجعولية الذاتية، ولا بالوجود ؛ لكونه صفة انتزاعية، فلا بد أن يتعلق باتصافها بالوجود، وإلا ارتفع الجعل رأسا ويرد عليه أولا أن الاتصاف أيضا انتزاعي. فإن قلت: مفاده أمر عيني ؟ قلت: هو نفس الماهية، كما بينا في الدليل الثاني. وثانيا: إن أريد بالمجعولية الذاتية ثبوت نفس الماهية لنفسها ففيه غفلة عن تصور معنى الجعل البسيط ، أو مجعولية مصداقه، وهو نفس الماهية، فلا استحالة فيه، بل هو أصل المسألة. ومن ههنا سقط ما قيل في إثبات لزوم المجعولية الذاتية أن حقيقتها مجعولة بثبوت الذات لنفسها باعتبار المصداق، ومصداقه ليس إلا نفس الماهية ، وقد قلتم إنها مجعولة. وثانيا إن المجعول بالذات ما هو ممكن بالذات، والإمكان كيفية النسبة. ويرد عليه أن المواد الثلاثة عندنا كيفيات نفس تقرر الماهية. وثالثا إن الجعل يستدعي مغايرة المجعول والمجعول إليه، ويرد عليه أن استدعاء المغايرة إنما هو في المؤلف، دون البسيط ؛ فإنه لا يستدعي مجعولا إليه ، فضلا عن المغايرة، والله أعلم.
Introduction of the book: [The impossibility of] the two opposites because they may be abstracted (intiza'i) thus outside the domain of the intellect. The removal of both opposites in the sense that neither one corresponds to what it reports is impossible, not that they are non-existent in external entities. How so? For if abstracted things had existence apart from the existence of the referent, it would entail the Necessary Being being a locus of accidents due to the daily occurrence of relations, and it would entail that one thing is described with infinite attributes because abstracted things may stop at a limit, like the chain of implications for example. Third: The essence is either in need of the creator primarily and essentially—which is what is sought—or accidentally, which entails the posteriority of the essence itself to the existing essence that is posterior to existence, or together with it, which entails the priority of the accident over the subject, or neither accidentally nor essentially, which entails the independence of the essence from the creator. And it is replied that the essence itself, by virtue of being determined by the creator, is posterior to the existing essence and prior to it in another mode of priority, and there is no impossibility in something posterior in one respect being prior in another respect. Also, if there were simultaneity between them, the priority of the accident over the subject would not necessarily follow, because what is simultaneous with what is essentially prior need not be prior. The cause is not impossible because it is not possible according to them; since the independence of the essence from the three modalities as qualities of the relation, so reflect. The followers of the Peripatetics said first: It is impossible to attach creation to essence, otherwise essential made-ness would follow; nor to existence because it is an abstract attribute; so it must be attached to its being described with existence, otherwise creation would be nullified. And it is replied first that being described is also abstract. If you say: Its purport is something concrete? I say: It is the essence itself, as we showed in the second proof. And second: If by essential made-ness is meant the affirmation of the essence itself to itself, then there is neglect of conceiving the meaning of simple creation; or the made-ness of its referent, which is the essence itself, so there is no impossibility in it; rather it is the very point of the issue. And from this falls what was said in establishing the necessity of essential made-ness: that its reality is made by the affirmation of the self to itself in terms of the referent, and its referent is nothing but the essence itself, and you have said that it is made. And second: That which is made in essence is that which is possible in essence, and possibility is a modality of the relation. And it is replied that the three modalities according to us are qualities of the very determination of the essence. And third: Creation requires a distinction between the made and the one to whom it is made, and it is replied that requiring distinction applies to the composite, not the simple; for it does not require a recipient, let alone distinction. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the Peripatetic (Mashsha'i) argument that creation (ja'l) cannot be attributed to essence or existence, but only to the attribute of being described by existence. The author first discusses a preliminary point about abstracted concepts (intiza'iyyat) and the impossibility of both opposites being absent. He then presents the Peripatetic trilemma: essence is either essentially in need of a creator (which is sought), accidentally in need, or not in need—if accidentally, the essence would be posterior to the existing essence; if simultaneously, an accident would precede its subject; if neither, the essence is independent. The author replies that the essence can be prior and posterior in different respects, and simultaneity does not entail priority of accident. Then he reports the Peripatetic claim that creation cannot attach to essence (otherwise essential made-ness) nor to existence (abstract), so it must attach to the 'being described' attribute. The author counters that 'being described' is also abstract, and that if the Peripatetics mean essential made-ness as self-affirmation, they misunderstand simple creation. The true referent of creation is the essence itself. The second Peripatetic point about possibility as a modal relation is rebutted by redefining the three modalities (necessity, possibility, impossibility) as qualities of the essence's determination. The third point about the need for distinction between maker and made is rejected for simple creation, which does not require a recipient. The argument uses technical distinctions familiar in Islamic philosophy and kalām, particularly regarding the nature of existence and essence.

Key Terms
الجعل (al-ja'l): The act of bringing something into existence (creation), often analyzed as simple (basiṭ) involving no recipient. [Note: In Peripatetic philosophy, ja'l often requires a recipient; here it is presented as simple, aligning with Ash'ari occasionalism.]
الماهية (al-māhiyya): Essence or quiddity; what something is in itself, distinct from existence. [Note: Stable term across traditions, but its reality is debated: Ash'ari holds it is the existent itself, while Peripatetics distinguish it from existence.]
المجعولية الذاتية (al-maj'ūliyya al-dhātiyya): The state of being made in one's essence; the author refutes that it implies circularity because simple creation makes the essence itself. [Note: This term is specific to the debate on creation, not commonly used outside metaphysics.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what are the three modalities?
A) Qualities of the relation.
B) Qualities of the essence's determination.
C) Attributes of existence.
D) Mental categories.

Key Takeaway
Modalities are not mere relations but real qualities of the essence's determination, grounding its need for a creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the statement 'The world is possible' – does this refer to a relation or a quality of the world's essence? Provide an argument based on the passage.

Refuting the Peripatetic Objection: Creation Requires Distinction Between Maker and Made
Author refutes three Peripatetic objections against attaching creation to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that creation requires a distinction between maker and made by distinguishing simple from composite creation.

Core Idea
Simple creation does not require a recipient; only composite acts do.

The third Peripatetic objection is that creation requires a distinction (mugāyara) between the made (maj'ūl) and the one to whom it is made (maj'ūl ilayh). The author replies that this requirement only holds for composite acts (al-mu'allaf), not for simple creation (al-ja'l al-basīṭ). This lesson examines this key distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the Peripatetic objection
The Peripatetics claim that any act of creation requires a distinction between the made and the recipient of creation.
2
Identify the author's reply
The author says that the demand for distinction applies only to composite acts, not to simple creation.
3
Define simple creation
Simple creation brings the entire essence into being without pre-existing parts or a substrate.
4
Apply the distinction
For simple creation, there is no 'recipient' distinct from the made; the essence itself is the product.

The Ash'ari Position on Existence and Essence
Author presents a later philosophical view and then declares the correct Ash'ari position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct Ash'ari view on the relationship between existence and essence, and distinguish it from the later philosophical view.

Core Idea
For Ash'aris, the existent is the essence itself, not a separate existence.

In this passage, the author reports a later philosophical view that separates existence from essence, claiming existence is the true reality and essence is only accidentally existent. He then declares the correct Ash'ari position: the existent (al-mawjūd) is the essence (al-māhiyya) itself. Understanding this distinction is crucial for Islamic metaphysics, especially the doctrine of creation (jaʿl) and divine attributes. Let's examine both views and grasp the Ash'ari resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the later view
The author says some later philosophers held that 'the true existent is existence (al-wujūd), distinct from essence (al-māhiyya), and essence is united with it in a kind of union, and is existent accidentally.' Note how they separate reality into two components.
2
Extract the Ash'ari counter-position
Contrast this with the author's declaration: 'the correct truth is that the existent is the essence.' This means the thing itself (the essence) is what exists, not some added property. The author attributes this to Imam al-Ashʿarī.
3
Understand key terms in context
Focus on three terms: al-wujūd (existence), al-māhiyya (essence), and al-majʿūl bi al-dhāt (that which is made essentially). The later view says the made thing is existence; the Ash'ari view implies it is the essence. Recognize the shift in meaning.
4
Connect to broader theological stakes
This debate affects how we understand God's creative act: if existence is distinct, then creation is giving existence to an essence; if existence is the essence, then creating the essence is creating the existent. The Ash'ari view affirms direct creation of objects, not abstract existences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه ذهب بعض المتأخرين إلى أن الموجود حقيقة هو الوجود مغايرا للماهية وهي متحدة معه نوع اتحاد، وموجودة بالعرض، والوجود متشخص بنفسه ، والمجعول بالذات هو الوجود جعلا بسيطا . وأورد عليه بيانات مطنبة، من أراد الاطلاع عليه(۱) فليرجع إلى كتبه، كـ «الأسفار» وحواشي «الشفاء» و«حكمة الإشراق». والحق الصحيح أن الموجود هو الماهية ، كما مرت الإشارة إليه آنفا، وإليه ذهب الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري قدس سره (۲) هو: على بن إسماعيل بن إسحاق، أبو الحسن الأشعري رضي الله عنه [ت: ٣٣٠هـ ] إمام أهل السنة والجماعة، ينتهي نسبه إلى الصحابي الجليل أبو موسى الأشعري رضي الله عنه. ولد بالبصرة وتوفي ببغداد انتهت إليه رئاسة الكلام بل الإمامة في الدين في عصره،
Then know that some later (philosophers) held that the true existent is existence, distinct from essence, and essence is united with it in a kind of union, and is existent accidentally, and existence is individuated by itself, and that which is made essentially is existence by a simple making. And lengthy discourses were objected to it; whoever wants to look into it should refer to his books, such as 'al-Asfār', glosses on 'al-Shifā'', and 'Ḥikmat al-Ishrāq'. And the correct truth is that the existent is the essence, as was indicated earlier, and to this went the Shaykh Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ash'arī, may Allah sanctify his secret. He is: 'Alī ibn Ismā'īl ibn Isḥāq, Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ash'arī, may Allah be pleased with him [d. 330 AH], the Imam of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jamā'a, his lineage ends with the noble companion Abū Mūsā al-Ash'arī, may Allah be pleased with him. He was born in Basra and died in Baghdad; the leadership of kalām, indeed the imamate in religion, culminated in him in his time.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage first reports a doctrine of some later philosophers (presumably from the Illuminationist or Peripatetic tradition) who assert that existence (al-wujūd) is the true reality, distinct from essence (al-māhiyya), and that essence is only accidentally existent through union with existence. They hold that existence is individuated by itself and is the direct object of simple creation (al-ja'l al-basīṭ). The author notes that lengthy objections have been raised against this view, and refers readers to major works like Mullā Ṣadrā's 'al-Asfār', the glosses on Avicenna's 'al-Shifā'', and Suhrawardī's 'Ḥikmat al-Ishrāq'. Then the author declares the correct position: the existent (al-mawjūd) is the essence itself, not something separate. He attributes this view to Imam Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ash'arī (d. 330 AH), the founder of Ash'ari theology, and provides a brief biographical note. This aligns with the earlier argument that the object of creation is the essence, not an abstract existence. The passage serves as a doctrinal resolution to the debate, grounding Islamic metaphysics in the Ash'ari tradition.

Key Terms
الوجود
الماهية
المجعول بالذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the correct view regarding the true existent (al-mawjūd)?
A) Existence is distinct from essence
B) Essence is accidentally existent
C) The existent is the essence itself
D) Existence is individuated by itself

Key Takeaway
The correct Ash'ari position is that the existent (al-mawjūd) is identical to the essence (al-māhiyya), rejecting the view that existence is a separate reality.

?

2) In your own words, explain why the Ash'ari position that 'the existent is the essence' is important for maintaining that God creates things directly, without intermediaries.

Refuting the Union Theory of Knowledge
Refutes the theory of union with the active intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical flaws in the claim that knowledge is union (ittihad) with the active intellect or the object.

Core Idea
If knowledge is union, then either nothing changes (making ignorance knowledge) or the intellect vanishes.

The passage challenges the idea that knowing something means becoming one with it. This theory, held by some philosophers, has serious logical consequences. We will walk through the refutation to see why union theories fail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial dilemma
The author first presents a dilemma: if all known things are in the active intellect, either we unite with all (yielding omniscience) or part (dividing the intellect). Both are problematic.
This sets up the refutation.
2
Examine the three possibilities after union
Assume union occurs. Then either (1) the intellect remains unchanged, making knowledge and ignorance the same; (2) something is nullified—either an attribute (transformation, not union) or the essence (intellect ceases); or (3) the intellect is perfected, leading to genus-species composition, not identity.
Each leads to absurdity.
3
Understand the genus-species objection
If union perfects the intellect, then the intellect becomes a genus and the object a differentia, making a composite. This contradicts the claim of simple unity.
This is a refined argument not in the Isharat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن كل المعلومات حاصلة فيها، فنحن إما مقارنون بالكل، فيلزم أن لا يكون شيء ما مجهولا لنا، أو بالبعض، فينقسم العقل الفعال.
وذهب جمع إلى أنه اتحاد مع العقل الفعال، وجمع إلى أنه اتحاد مع المعلوم. قال الشيخ وكان رجل يقال له فرفوريوس يفرط في هذا الرأي، وهما أيضا باطلان؛ لأن العاقل إذا اتحد مع المعقول أو العقل الفعال فإما بقي كما كان، فحال العلم والجهل سواء، وإما بطل عنه شيء، فالباطل إما صفته، فيكون استحالته لا اتحادا، أو ذاته، فيلزم عدم العاقل عند التعقل، وإما كمل، فإن كمل ذاته كمالا نوعيا فيكون العاقل جنسا، والعقل أو المعقول فصلا، والمجموع نوعا مركبا منهما، أو صفته فيكون كونا لها لا اتحادا. وهذا التقرير أجمع للشقوق مما في «الإشارات»، وههنا برهان آخر، سيجيئ إن شاء الله تعالى.
والمشهور من الحكماء أن الصورة الحاضرة إما عين المعلوم بالذات، كما عليه الجمهور، أو شبحه المغاير بالذات، كما يفهم من ظاهر عبارات الشيخ المقتول، وهو مختار سيد العلماء، سند الأتقياء، ذي الجهاد الأكبر، المطلع على أسرار رب العزة، أبي وأستاذي نظام الملة والدين. والدليل عليه ورود إشكالات غير مندفعة على أصحاب الاتحاد بالذات بين العلم والمعلوم، كما يظهر إن شاء الله.
Because all known things are contained in it, we are either united with all of it, which would necessitate that nothing is unknown to us, or with part of it, which would divide the active intellect. Some held that it is union with the active intellect, and some that it is union with the known. The Shaykh said: there was a man called Porphyry who exaggerated this opinion, and both are false. Because if the intellect unites with the intelligible or the active intellect, then either it remains as it was, so the state of knowledge and ignorance are equal; or something is nullified from it, so the nullified thing is either its attribute, so it is transformation, not union; or its essence, so the non-existence of the intellect follows upon intellection; or it is perfected, so if its essence is perfected with a specific perfection, then the intellect would be a genus, and the intellect or intelligible a differentia, and the composite a species composed of them; or if its attribute is perfected, then it would be a becoming for it, not union. This exposition is more comprehensive of the cases than what is in the 'Isharat, and here is another proof, will come if Allah wills. And the well-known among the philosophers is that the present form is either the object itself in essence, as the majority hold, or its phantom different in essence, as understood from the apparent expressions of the martyred shaykh, and it is the choice of the master of scholars, the support of the pious, the one of greatest jihad, the one informed of the secrets of the Lord of might, my father and teacher, Nazam al-Milla wa al-Din. The evidence for it is the occurrence of irrefutable objections against the proponents of essential union between knowledge and the known, as will appear if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage critiques the theory that knowledge consists in union (ittihad) with the active intellect or with the object. The author first presents the claim that if all known things are contained in the active intellect, then either we are united with all of it (leading to omniscience) or only part (dividing the intellect). He then refutes both views: if the intellect unites with the object, either it remains unchanged (so knowledge and ignorance are the same), or something is nullified—if it is an attribute, that is transformation not union; if it is the essence, the intellect vanishes; or if it is perfected, then the union would be a genus-species composition, not identity. The author then states the correct view: the mental form (sura hadira) is either the object itself (as the majority hold) or a phantom (shabah) distinct from it (the view preferred by the author). This is supported by the fact that objections against the identity theory are insurmountable.

Key Terms
اتحاد
عقل فعال
فرفوريوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, if the intellect unites with the object and remains unchanged, what is the consequence?
A) The intellect becomes a genus
B) Knowledge and ignorance become identical
C) The object is divided
D) The intellect vanishes

Key Takeaway
The union theory of knowledge fails logically because it leads to contradiction or reduction ad absurdum in every case.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a similar refutation against someone who claims that understanding Allah (ma'rifah) is literally union (ittihad) with Him. Use the same four-case dilemma.
